NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
NOTE_ID: note_330	SOURCE_FILE: note_330.txt
INDICATION FOR OPERATION: [REDACTED] is a 60 year old-year-old male who presents with worsening dyspnea on exertion and wheezing.  The nature, purpose, risks, benefits and alternatives to Bronchoscopy were discussed with the patient in detail.  Patient indicated a wish to proceed with surgery and informed consent was signed.
 
CONSENT : Obtained before the procedure. Its indications and potential complications and alternatives were discussed with the patient or surrogate. The patient or surrogate read and signed the provided consent form / provided consent over the phone. The consent was witnessed by an assisting medical professional.
 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: J98.09 Other diseases of bronchus, not elsewhere classified
 
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  J98.09 Other diseases of bronchus, not elsewhere classified
 
PROCEDURE:  
31645 Therapeutic aspiration initial episode
31624 Dx bronchoscope/lavage (BAL)    
31630 Balloon dilation
31636 Dilate and bronchial stent initial bronchus
31640 Bronchoscopy with excision 
31641 Destruction of tumor OR relief of stenosis by any method other than excision (eg. laser therapy, cryotherapy)
31635 Foreign body removal
 
22 Substantially greater work than normal (i.e., increased intensity, time, technical difficulty of procedure, and severity of patient's condition, physical and mental effort required)
 
IP UCSD CODE MOD DETAILS: 
Unusual Procedure:
This patient required a pt with complex stenosis, post obstructive pneumonia with bleeding airways. The airways required multiple dilation to remove foreign body . This resulted in >50% increased work due to Increased intensity, Technical difficulty of procedure, and Physical and mental effort required. Apply to: 31630 Balloon dilation
31636 Dilate and bronchial stent initial bronchus
31635 Foreign body removal. 
 
ANESTHESIA: 
Local anesthesia with: SEE MAR
 
MONITORING : Pulse oximetry, heart rate, telemetry, and BP were continuously monitored by an independent trained observer that was present throughout the entire procedure.
 
INSTRUMENT : 
Rigid Bronchoscope
Flexible Therapeutic Bronchoscope
Flexible Hybrid (Pedatric) Bronchoscope
 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS:   Minimum
 
COMPLICATIONS:    None
 
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After the successful induction of anesthesia, a timeout was performed (confirming the patient's name, procedure type, and procedure location).
 
Initial Airway Inspection Findings:
The patient was sedated and an iGel was placed by anesthesia. The bronchoscope was advanced to the level of the vocal cords. The vocal cords are normal in structure. A total of 6 mL of 1% lidocaine was instilled onto the vocal cords. The bronchoscope was advanced through the vocal cords into the trachea. 
 
The airways were examined to the subsegmental level bilaterally. The Right anastomosis was intact without stenosis. The LMSB had stenosis just distal to the anastomosis. The stenosis was approximately 4 mm and the therapeutic and P190 bronchoscope could not be advanced through the stenosis. The stent was seen distal to the stenosis. Proximal to the stenosis the airway had some malacia
 
The iGel was removed and the patient was intubated atraumatically with a black ventilating rigid bronchoscope. 
 
Balloon dilation was performed at Left Mainstem.  6/7/8 Elation balloon was used to perform dilation to 8 mm at the Left Mainstem.  Total 3 inflations with dilation time of 30 seconds each. After dilation the P-190 bronchoscope could be advanced through the stenosis. 
 
The stent was seen distal to the stenosis and the LUL was occluded by the stent. Using the bronchoscope the stent was lifted and a large amount of white-yellow pus was therapeutically aspirated. 
 
Bronchial alveolar lavage was performed at Anterior Segment of LUL (LB3).  Instilled 40 cc of NS, suction returned with 15 cc of NS.  Samples sent for Cell Count and Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal).
 
Endobronchial tumor was noted and excised with mechanical debridement from the LMSB. 
 
The proximal end of the stent was now able to be visualized. Using rat tooth forceps the stent was grasped and removed enbloc through the rigid bronchoscope. No residual material was left in the airway
 
Endobronchial obstruction at Left Mainstem was treated with the following modalities:
 

Modality	Tools	Setting/Mode	Duration	Results
Electrocautery	 	 	 	 
APC	 	 	 	 
Laser	 	 	 	 
CoreCath	 	 	 	 
Cryoprobe	1.1	10 -30 second freeze thaw cycles	Total of 6 treatments	Improvement in airway diameter to 8mm
 
Prior to treatment, affected airway was note to be 20% patent.  After treatment, the airway was 60% patent. 
 
Balloon dilation was performed at Left Mainstem.  6/7/8 Elation balloon was used to perform dilation to 8 mm at the Left Mainstem.  Total 2 inflations with dilation time of 60 seconds each. After this dilation the therapeutic bronchoscope could be advanced through the stenosis.
 
The following stent (Bona stent 10 x 30) was placed in the Left Mainstem. 
 
 
The patient tolerated the procedure well.  There were no immediate complications.  At the conclusion of the operation, the patient was extubated in the operating room and transported to the recovery room in stable condition. 
 
SPECIMEN(S): 
BAL - LUL
Foreign body removal - path
LMSB bronchus tissue/tumor path
 
IMPRESSION/PLAN:[REDACTED] is a 60 year old-year-old male who presents for bronchoscopy for worsening dyspnea on exertion, wheezing and difficulty with getting mucus out. Stent found have migrated distally with airway obstruction of the LUL and post obstructive pneumonia. 
Pt to be admitted for IV antibiotics 
Please resume stent hygiene with albuterol neb, followed by 3% saline nebulizer. This should be done TID. 
Add guaifenesin 1200 mg po BID
Please keep NPO after midnight until pulmonary team is able to see patient to assess if additional bronchoscopy is needed
CXR in PACU

NOTE: note_285

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
NOTE_ID: note_285	SOURCE_FILE: note_285.txt
INDICATION FOR OPERATION:  [REDACTED]  s is a 44 year old-year-old female who presents with inter and intralobular septal thickening as well as groundglass opacities.  The nature, purpose, risks, benefits and alternatives to Bronchoscopy were discussed with the patient in detail.  Patient indicated a wish to proceed with surgery and informed consent was signed.
 
CONSENT : Obtained before the procedure. Its indications and potential complications and alternatives were discussed with the patient or surrogate. The patient or surrogate read and signed the provided consent form / provided consent over the phone. The consent was witnessed by an assisting medical professional.
 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: R91.8 Other nonspecific abnormal finding of lung field.
 
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  R91.8 Other nonspecific abnormal finding of lung field.
 
PROCEDURE:  
31645 Therapeutic aspiration initial episode
31624 Dx bronchoscope/lavage (BAL)    
31628 TBBX single lobe     
31629 TBNA single lobe   
31627 Navigational Bronchoscopy (computer assisted)
77012 Radiology / radiologic guidance for CT guided needle placement (CIOS)
76377 3D rendering with interpretation and reporting of CT, US, Tomo modality (ION Planning Station)
31652 EBUS sampling 1 or 2 nodes
31654 Radial EBUS for peripheral lesion
76981 Ultrasound Elastography, Parenchyma of Organ
 
22 Substantially greater work than normal (i.e., increased intensity, time, technical difficulty of procedure, and severity of patient's condition, physical and mental effort required)
 
IP UCSD CODE MOD DETAILS: 
Unusual Procedure:
This patient required a Multiple Bronchoalveolar lavages in different locations and elastography evaluation of multiple lymph node stations. This resulted in >50% increased work due to Time, Technical difficulty of procedure, and Physical and mental effort required. Apply to: 31624 Dx bronchoscope/lavage (BAL)    
76981 Ultrasound Elastography, Parenchyma of Organ
76982 Ultrasound Elastography, First Target Lesion. 
 

 
ANESTHESIA: 
General Anesthesia
 
MONITORING : Pulse oximetry, heart rate, telemetry, and BP were continuously monitored by an independent trained observer that was present throughout the entire procedure.
 
INSTRUMENT : 
Flexible Therapeutic Bronchoscope
Linear EBUS 
Radial EBUS
Ion Robotic Bronchoscope
 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS:   Moderate
 
COMPLICATIONS:    None
 
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After the successful induction of anesthesia, a timeout was performed (confirming the patient's name, procedure type, and procedure location).
 
Initial Airway Inspection Findings:
 
Entire airway normal (via ETT)
The endotracheal tube is in good position. The visualized portion of the trachea is of normal caliber. The carina is sharp. The tracheobronchial tree was examined to at least the first subsegmental level. Bronchial mucosa and anatomy are normal; there are no endobronchial lesions. Airway exam notable for mild mucus/secretions bilaterally. 
 
Successful therapeutic aspiration was performed to clean out the Trachea (Distal 1/3), Right Mainstem, Bronchus Intermedius , Left Mainstem, Carina, RUL Carina (RC1), RML Carina (RC2), LUL Lingula Carina (Lc1), and Left Carina (LC2) from mucus. 
 
CT Chest scan was placed on separate planning station to generate 3D rendering of the pathway to target.   The navigational plan was reviewed and verified.  This was then loaded into robotic bronchoscopy platform. 
 
Ventilation Parameters:
Mode	RR	TV	PEEP	FiO2	Flow Rate	Pmean
VCV	12	300	12	10	100	15
 
Robotic navigation bronchoscopy was performed with Ion platform.  Partial registration was used.    Ion robotic catheter was used to engage the Anterior Segment of RUL (RB3).  Target lesion is about 1 cm in diameter.   Under navigational guidance the ion robotic catheter was advanced to 1.0 cm away from the planned target. 
 
Radial EBUS was performed to confirm that the location of the nodule is Concentric.  The following features were noted: Blizzard Sign (GGO).
 
Cone Beam CT was performed: 3-D reconstructions were performed on an independent workstation.  Cios Spin system was used for evaluation of nodule location.  Low dose spin was performed to acquire CT imaging.  This was passed on to Ion platform system for reconstruction and nodule location.  The 3D images was interpreted on an independent workstation (Ion).   Using the newly acquired nodule location, the Ion robotic system was adjusted to the new targeted location. I personally interpreted the cone beam CT and 3-D reconstruction. 
 
The robotic catheter was then advanced near the newly segmented lesion. Cone Beam CT was performed: 3-D reconstructions were performed on an independent workstation.  Cios Spin system was used for evaluation of nodule location.  Low dose spin was performed to acquire CT imaging.  This was passed on to Ion platform system for reconstruction and nodule location.  The 3D images was interpreted on an independent workstation (Ion).   Images showed tool-in-lesion. I personally interpreted the cone beam CT and 3-D reconstruction. 
 

 
Transbronchial needle aspiration was performed with 21G Needle and 23G Needle through the extended working channel catheter.  Total 6 samples were collected.  Samples sent for Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal) and Cytology.
 
Transbronchial cryobiopsy was performed with 1.1mm cryoprobe via the extended working channel catheter.  Freeze time of 6 seconds were used.  Total 7 samples were collected.  Samples sent for Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal) and Pathology.
 
Bronchial alveolar lavage (mini-BAL) was performed the extended working channel catheter.  Instilled 20 cc of NS, suction returned with 5 cc of NS.  Samples sent for Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal).
 
Bronchial alveolar lavage was performed at Apical Segment of RUL (RB1), Posterior Segment of RUL (RB2), and Anterior Segment of RUL (RB3).  Instilled 60 cc of NS, suction returned with 20 cc of NS.  Samples sent for Cell Count, Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal), and Cytology.
 
ROSE from ION procedure was noted to be:
Inflammatory cells; No evidence of a malignant neoplasm
 
EBUS-Findings
Indications: Diagnostic
Technique:
All lymph node stations were assessed. Only those 5 mm or greater in short axis were sampled.
 
Lymph node sizing was performed by EBUS and sampling by transbronchial needle aspiration was performed using 22-gauge Needle.
 
Lymph Nodes/Sites Inspected: 4R (lower paratracheal) node
4L (lower paratracheal) node
7 (subcarinal) node
11Rs lymph node
11Ri lymph node
11L lymph node
 
No immediate complications
 
Endobronchial ultrasound (EBUS) elastography was performed to assess lymph node stiffness and tissue characteristics. Elastography provided a semi-quantitative classification (Type 1 3), which was used to guide biopsy site selection and sampling strategy. 
 
Lymph Nodes Evaluated:
Site 1: The 4L (lower paratracheal) node was < 10 mm on CT  and Metabolic activity unknown or PET-CT scan unavailable. The lymph node was photographed. The site was sampled.. 4 endobronchial ultrasound guided transbronchial biopsies were performed with samples obtained. Endobronchial ultrasound (EBUS) elastography was performed to assess lymph node stiffness and tissue characteristics. The target lymph node demonstrated a Type 1 elastographic pattern, predominantly soft (green/yellow), suggesting a reactive or benign process. Despite the benign appearance, TBNA was performed to confirm the absence of malignancy and to obtain cytology for diagnostic completeness.
 
The patient tolerated the procedure well.  There were no immediate complications.  At the conclusion of the operation, the patient was extubated in the operating room and transported to the recovery room in stable condition. 
 
SPECIMEN(S): 
- RUL nodule TBNA (cyto and micro), TBCBx (path and micro)
- RUL BAL 
- Station 4L TBNA 
 
 
IMPRESSION/PLAN:  [REDACTED]   is a 44 year old-year-old female who presents for bronchoscopy for evaluation of diffuse groundglass opacities. The patient underwent robot-assisted bronchoscopy and endobronchial ultrasound with transbronchial needle aspiration without immediate complication.
 
PLAN
--Post-procedure CXR
--Follow-up cyto, micro, path results
--Continued care per primary team

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
NOTE_ID: note_342	SOURCE_FILE: note_342.txt
INDICATION FOR OPERATION: [REDACTED] is a 69 year old-year-old male who presents with bronchial stenosis.  The nature, purpose, risks, benefits and alternatives to Bronchoscopy were discussed with the patient in detail.  Patient indicated a wish to proceed with surgery and informed consent was signed.
 
CONSENT : Obtained before the procedure. Its indications and potential complications and alternatives were discussed with the patient or surrogate. The patient or surrogate read and signed the provided consent form / provided consent over the phone. The consent was witnessed by an assisting medical professional.
 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: J98.09 Other diseases of bronchus, not elsewhere classified
 
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  J98.09 Other diseases of bronchus, not elsewhere classified
 
PROCEDURE:  
31645 Therapeutic aspiration initial episode
31622 Dx bronchoscope/cell washing          
31624 Dx bronchoscope/lavage (BAL)    
31625 Endobronchial Biopsy(s)
31628 TBBX single lobe     
31630 Balloon dilation
31641 Destruction of tumor OR relief of stenosis by any method other than excision (eg. laser therapy, cryotherapy)
 
General Anesthesia

 
ANESTHESIA: 
Local anesthesia with: SEE MAR
 
MONITORING : Pulse oximetry, heart rate, telemetry, and BP were continuously monitored by an independent trained observer that was present throughout the entire procedure.
 
INSTRUMENT : 
Flexible Therapeutic Bronchoscope
 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS:   30mL
 
COMPLICATIONS:    None
 
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After the successful induction of anesthesia, a timeout was performed (confirming the patient's name, procedure type, and procedure location).
 
Initial Airway Inspection Findings:
 
The flexible therapeutic bronchoscope was inserted into the LMA and advanced through the vocal cords into the airway. Bilateral airway inspection showed complex stenosis and malacic area at anastomosis on left mainstem. Right anastomosis was normal with a clip visible in the airway lumen. The anatomic segmental branching was normal. There was granulation tissue partially obstruction left anastomosis from 10 o clock to 5 o clock position. 
 
Endobronchial biopsy was performed at Left Mainstem anastomosis.  Lesion was successfully removed.  Samples sent for Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal) and Pathology.
 
Endobronchial obstruction at Left Mainstem was treated with the following modalities:
 
Modality	Tools	Setting/Mode	Duration	Results
Electrocautery	 	 	 	 
APC	 	 	 	 
Laser	 	 	 	 
CoreCath	 	 	 	 
Cryoprobe	2.4mm	30 s freeze and thaw cycle 4 applications 10 o clock, 12 o clock 2o clock 4 o clock	 	Improved luminal patency
 
Balloon dilation was performed at Left Mainstem.  6/7/8 Elation balloon was used to perform dilation to 8 mm at the Left Mainstem.  Total 3 inflations with dilation time of 60s seconds each.
 
Prior to treatment, affected airway was note to be 60% patent.  After treatment, the airway was 80% patent. 
 
Transbronchial biopsy was performed with alligator forceps at Anteromedial Segment of LLL (Lb7/8) and Lateral-basal Segment of LLL (LB9).  Total 8 samples were collected.  Samples sent for Pathology. 
 
Bronchial alveolar lavage was performed at Superior Segment of Lingula (LB4) and Inferior Segment of Lingula (LB5).  Instilled 60 cc of NS, suction returned with 20 cc of NS.  Samples sent for Cell Count, Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal), and Cytology.
 
The patient tolerated the procedure well.  There were no immediate complications.  At the conclusion of the operation, the patient was extubated in the operating room and transported to the recovery room in stable condition. 
 
SPECIMEN(S): 
 
LLL TBBx
LMSB EBBx
Lingula BAL
 
IMPRESSION/PLAN:[REDACTED] is a 69 year old-year-old male who presents for bronchoscopy for bronchial stenosis and Tbbx to rule out rejection
 
[ ] cxr in pacu
[ ] Stenosis is complex and partially malacic with some granulation tissue. Will likely need a stent trial in short interval, follow up in clinic

NOTE_ID: note_355	SOURCE_FILE: note_355.txt
INDICATION FOR OPERATION: [REDACTED]is a 85 year old male who presents with Pleural Effusion.  
 
CONSENT : Obtained before the procedure. The nature, indications, purpose, benefits, risks, potential complications, and alternatives to Chest Ultrasound and Thoracentesis were discussed with the patient or surrogate decision-maker in detail.  Patient or surrogate decision-maker agreed to proceed with procedure.  The patient or surrogate decision-maker read and signed the provided consent form or provided consent over the phone. If consent was provided over the phone, then the consent was witnessed by an assisting medical professional.
 
All procedure related images were saved and archived in Media folder on Onedrive behind UCSD firewall, relevant images are also uploaded to PACS system or in the media section of the patient's chart.
 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Pleural Effusion
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Same as preoperative diagnosis - see above. 
 
PROCEDURE:  
76604 Ultrasound, chest (includes mediastinum), real time with image documentation
32555 Aspirate pleura with imaging (thoracentesis)
 
50 Bilateral Procedures (Procedure done on both sides of the body) and 59 Similar to 51 but for uncommonly combined procedures. Can be used if a diagnostic procedure is performed which provides information which leads to a therapeutic procedure (XE/XS/XP/XU)
 
IP UCSD CODE MOD DETAILS: Unusual Procedure (50 MODIFIER):
This patient required a bilateral procedure today when this procedure would typically be unilateral. Apply to:
76604 Ultrasound, chest (includes mediastinum), real time with image documentation
 
59 MODIFIER:
This thoracentesis procedure was performed in addition to the bronchoscopy procedure.  These are separate and uncommonly combined procedures.  This thoracentesis was performed in the pre-operative area.  The patient was then taken to a different location (the operative area) and underwent bronchoscopy procedure  please see separate documentation for that procedure.
 
Local Anesthesia (Lidocaine)
 
 
MONITORING : Pulse oximetry, heart rate, telemetry, and BP were continuously monitored by an independent trained observer that was present throughout the entire procedure.
 
PROCEDURE(S) IN DETAIL:
A timeout was performed (confirming the patient's name, MRN, DOB, procedure type, and procedure location).
 
PATIENT POSITION:  Sitting
 
LEFT CHEST ULTRASOUND PROCEDURE:
FINDINGS:
Hemithorax:  LEFT
Pleural Effusion: 
Volume:  Small
Echogenicity:  Anechoic
Loculations:  None
Diaphragmatic Motion:  Normal
Lung: 
Lung sliding before procedure:  Present
Lung sliding post procedure:  See other ultrasound exam below
Lung consolidation/atelectasis:  Present - very minimal at lung base consistent with atelectasis
Pleura:  Normal
Image(s) saved and uploaded:  YES - saved to Media tab
 
RIGHT CHEST ULTRASOUND PROCEDURE:
FINDINGS:
Hemithorax:  RIGHT
Pleural Effusion: 
Volume:  Tiny - not amenable to thoracentesis
Echogenicity:  Anechoic
Loculations:  None
Diaphragmatic Motion:  Normal
Lung: 
Lung sliding before procedure:  Present
Lung sliding post procedure:  N/A
Lung consolidation/atelectasis:  Present - tiny at lung base, consistent with atelectasis.
Pleura:  Normal
Image(s) saved and uploaded:  YES - saved to Media tab
 
LEFT THORACENTESIS PROCEDURE:
Anatomic landmarks and ultrasound-guidance were utilized to determine the appropriate insertion site.  Insertion site marked.  Thoracentesis Kit was used. 
 
ANESTHESIA:   Lidocaine 1%: 10 mL      Other:  
 
Entry Site: LEFT 7th Intercostal Space in the Mid-scapular line
 
Procedure was performed using sterile technique throughout.  Insertion site prepped and draped in sterile fashion.  1% lidocaine was used to anesthesize the skin, subcutaneous tissue, superior aspect of the inferior rib periosteum and parietal pleura. A #10 scalpel blade was used to nick the skin at the insertion site.  A Cook 5Fr Yueh over-the-needle catheter was inserted using the Seldinger technique. The needle and over-the-needle catheter were introduced through the skin incision into the pleural space while applying negative aspiration pressure.  Entry into pleural space was confirmed by aspiration of light yellow-colored fluid.  While holding the insertion needle stable, the catheter was then threaded into the pleural space without difficulty.  The insertion needle was removed.  Pleural fluid was aspirated through the catheter via manual aspiration without difficulty - see fluid description and aspirated volume below.  The catheter was then removed while patient exhaled.  Pressure briefly held until minimal bleeding stopped and bandage applied over site.
 
Fluid Description:  Light yellow Serous
Fluid Volume Removed: 250 ml 
 
Drainage method:   Manual aspiration into drainage bag.
Pleural pressures:   Not measured.
 
Reason pleural fluid aspiration was stopped:  Unable to manually aspirate any further fluid.
 
Post-procedure Chest Ultrasound (after thoracentesis catheter removed) showed: 
LEFT CHEST ULTRASOUND PROCEDURE:
FINDINGS:
Hemithorax:  LEFT
Pleural Effusion: 
Volume:  Very Small
Echogenicity:  Anechoic
Loculations:  None
Diaphragmatic Motion:  Normal
Lung: 
Lung sliding before procedure:  See other ultrasound exam above
Lung sliding post procedure:  Present
Lung consolidation/atelectasis:  Present - tiny at lung base, consistent with atelectasis.
Pleura:  Normal
Image(s) saved and uploaded:  YES - saved to the Media tab.
 
SPECIMEN(S): 
?Analyses - TProt, LDH, Glucose, and Cholesterol
?Cell Count
?Cultures - Gram Stain/Bacterial Culture, Blood culture bottle bedside innoculation, AFB, and Fungal
?Cytology  

 
CXR ordered: yes
 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS:  <5 mL
COMPLICATIONS:  None.  There were no immediate complications.
 
IMPRESSION/PLAN:[REDACTED]is a 85 year old-year-old male who presents for Chest Ultrasound and Thoracentesis.  The patient tolerated the procedure well.  
 
DISPOSITION: To remain in same location - same level of care
 
Follow-up pleural fluid studies.
To proceed with robotic navigational bronchoscopy procedure next.

NOTE: note_312

NOTE TEXT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
NOTE_ID: note_312	SOURCE_FILE: note_312.txt
INDICATION FOR OPERATION:  [REDACTED]is a 70 year old-year-old male who presents with left anastomotic stenosis.  The nature, purpose, risks, benefits and alternatives to Bronchoscopy were discussed with the patient in detail.  Patient indicated a wish to proceed with surgery and informed consent was signed.
 
CONSENT : Obtained before the procedure. Its indications and potential complications and alternatives were discussed with the patient or surrogate. The patient or surrogate read and signed the provided consent form / provided consent over the phone. The consent was witnessed by an assisting medical professional.
 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Left anastomotic dehiscence 
 
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Left anastomotic dehiscence 
 
PROCEDURE:  
31645 Therapeutic aspiration initial episode
31624 Dx bronchoscope/lavage (BAL)    
31625 Endobronchial Biopsy(s)
31630 Balloon dilation
31640 Bronchoscopy with excision 
31641 Destruction of tumor OR relief of stenosis by any method other than excision (eg. laser therapy, cryotherapy)
 
 
ANESTHESIA: 
Local anesthesia with: SEE MAR
 
MONITORING : Pulse oximetry, heart rate, telemetry, and BP were continuously monitored by an independent trained observer that was present throughout the entire procedure.
 
INSTRUMENT : 
Flexible Therapeutic Bronchoscope
 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS:   Minimum
 
COMPLICATIONS:    None
 
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
After the successful induction of anesthesia, a timeout was performed (confirming the patient's name, procedure type, and procedure location).
 
Initial Airway Inspection Findings:
 
The patient was sedated and an iGel was placed by anesthesia. The bronchoscope was introduced into the iGel and advanced to the level of the vocal cords. A total of 4 mL of 2% lidocaine was instilled into the vocal cords. 
 
The bronchoscope was advanced through vocal cords into the trachea. There were several areas consistent with TPO. The right anastomosis has a staple herniating through at the 1 o'clock position. There was no evidence of dehiscence.  The left anastomosis was covered by a bona stent. The stent was in adequate position. The distal end of the stent had some granulation tissue and stenosis. 
The RUL anterior segment had narrowing due to collapse of cartilage.
 
Successful therapeutic aspiration was performed to clean out the Trachea (Middle 1/3), Trachea (Distal 1/3), and Left Mainstem from mucus. 
 
Bronchial alveolar lavage was performed at Apical-Posterior Segment of LUL (LB1/2).  Instilled 60 cc of NS, suction returned with 30 cc of NS.  Samples sent for Cell Count and Microbiology (Cultures/Viral/Fungal).
 
Endobronchial obstruction at distal LMSB was treated with the following modalities:
 

Modality	Tools	Setting/Mode	Duration	Results
Electrocautery	 	 	 	 
APC	1.5	25W/2	 	 
Laser	 	 	 	 
CoreCath	 	 	 	 
Cryoprobe	2.4	 	10 seconds	 
 
Prior to treatment, affected airway was note to be 90% patent.  After treatment, the airway was 95% patent. 
 
Endobronchial tumor was noted and excised with mechanical debridement with forceps and this was send for pathology. There was no evidence of active bleeding and the bronchoscope was removed. 
 
Balloon dilation was performed at distal LMSB.  10/11/12 Elation balloon was used to perform dilation to 11 mm at the distal LMSB.  Total 2 inflations with dilation time of 60 seconds each.
 
 
The patient tolerated the procedure well.  There were no immediate complications.  At the conclusion of the operation, the patient was extubated in the operating room and transported to the recovery room in stable condition. 
 
SPECIMEN(S): 
BAL LUL
Endobronchial tissue distal LMSB
 
IMPRESSION/PLAN: [REDACTED]is a 70 year old-year-old male who presents for bronchoscopy for tracheal stenosis s/p stenting on 1/5/2024.
Stent check/removal in 4 weeks

NOTE_ID:  note_272 SOURCE_FILE: note_272.txt 
INTERVENTIONAL PULMONOLOGY OPERATIVE REPORT
 
DATE OF PROCEDURE: [REDACTED]
 
 
INDICATION FOR OPERATION:  [REDACTED]is a 33 year old-year-old female who presents with hemoptysis and respiratory failure.  The nature, purpose, risks, benefits and alternatives to Bronchoscopy were discussed with the patient in detail.  Patient indicated a wish to proceed with surgery and informed consent was signed.
 
CONSENT : Obtained before the procedure. Its indications and potential complications and alternatives were discussed with the patient or surrogate. The patient or surrogate read and signed the provided consent form / provided consent over the phone. The consent was witnessed by an assisting medical professional.
 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: R91.8 Other nonspecific abnormal finding of lung field.
 
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  R91.8 Other nonspecific abnormal finding of lung field.
 
PROCEDURE:  
31645 Therapeutic aspiration initial episode
 
ATTENDING:  
[REDACTED]
 
ANESTHESIA: 
Continued IV infusions with 2 mg dilaudid bolus
 
 
MONITORING : Pulse oximetry, heart rate, telemetry, and BP were continuously monitored by an independent trained observer that was present throughout the entire procedure.
 
INSTRUMENT : 
Disposable Bronchoscope
 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS:   Minimum
 
COMPLICATIONS:    None
 
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
 images are also uploaded to PACS system or in the media section of the patient's chart. 
 
PATIENT POSITION: Supine
 
Initial Airway Inspection Findings:
 
The tracheostomy tube is in good position.
Pharynx: Not assessed due to bronchoscopy introduction through tracheostomy tube.
Larynx: Not assessed due to bronchoscopy introduction through tracheostomy tube.
Vocal Cords: Not assessed due to bronchoscopy introduction through tracheostomy tube.
Trachea: Distal 1/3 normal.
Main Carina: Sharp
Right Lung Proximal Airways: Bloody secretions and blood clot noted at right-sided airways, particularly RML and RB6 subsegment. Otherwise, normal anatomic branching to segmental level.  No evidence of mass, lesions, or other endobronchial pathology.
Left Lung Proximal Airways: Stent well-seated at LMSB with distal end at LLL truncus basalis. Moderate bloody as well as clear secretions. LUL and LB6 jailed off by stent, otherwise normal anatomic branching to segmental level.
Mucosa: Normal.
Secretions: Minimal, thin, and clear with some blood.  
 
Successful therapeutic aspiration was performed to clean out the Trachea (Distal 1/3), Right Mainstem, Bronchus Intermedius , Left Mainstem, Carina, RUL Carina (RC1), and RML Carina (RC2) from mucus, blood, and blood clots. 
 
Blood secretions in the RML
Thin, white-yellow mucus in the LLL antero-medial, lateral and posterior segments
Defect seen in stent at 2 o'clock position with bubbling from it
 
The patient tolerated the procedure well.  There were no immediate complications.  At the conclusion of the operation, the patient was in stable condition. 
 
SPECIMEN(S): 
--None
 
IMPRESSION/PLAN: [REDACTED]is a 33 year old-year-old female who presents for bronchoscopy for evaluation of airways and reassessment of stent position and hemoptysis. Tolerated the procedure well and there were no immediate complications.
 
--Plan for repeat bronchoscopy in OR later this week for endobronchial blocker placement (plan for Amplatzer vascular plug)
--Continue stent hydration
--Continued care per primary team
